  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ac46342d-39a3-4986-a9ce-4ff9d8e23341'

<span id="freeTextContainer16196740926585533494">London, 1861.<br/><br/>Sir Richard Francis Burton—explorer, linguist, scholar, and swordsman; his reputation tarnished; his career in tatters; his former partner missing and probably dead.<br/><br/>Algernon Charles Swinburne—unsuccessful poet and follower of de Sade; for whom pain is pleasure, and brandy is ruin!<br/><br/>They stand at a crossroads in their lives and are caught in the epicenter of an e</span>
  <span id="freeText16196740926585533494" style="display:none">London, 1861.<br /><br />Sir Richard Francis Burton—explorer, linguist, scholar, and swordsman; his reputation tarnished; his career in tatters; his former partner missing and probably dead.<br /><br />Algernon Charles Swinburne—unsuccessful poet and follower of de Sade; for whom pain is pleasure, and brandy is ruin!<br /><br />They stand at a crossroads in their lives and are caught in the epicenter of an empire torn by conflicting forces: Engineers transform the landscape with bigger, faster, noisier, and dirtier technological wonders; Eugenicists develop specialist animals to provide unpaid labor; Libertines oppose repressive laws and demand a society based on beauty and creativity; while the Rakes push the boundaries of human behavior to the limits with magic, drugs, and anarchy. The two men are sucked into the perilous depths of this moral and ethical vacuum when Lord Palmerston commissions Burton to investigate assaults on young women committed by a weird apparition known as Spring Heeled Jack, and to find out why werewolves are terrorizing London's East End.<br /><br />Their investigations lead them to one of the defining events of the age, and the terrifying possibility that the world they inhabit shouldn't exist at all!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16196740926585533494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_103632516" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103632516" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103632516?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-philip-k-dick">award-nominee-philip-k-dick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=alternative-history">alternative-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=sherlockian">sherlockian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=punked">punked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103632516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5902805253272671695">This super debut novel is like a sweet, dainty cup of mild <b>English tea</b>...if it was spiked with <b>Absinthe</b>, poured into a <b>heavy brass goblet</b> and served with <b>Laudanum-laced</b> cookies shaped like medical experiments gone awry. In other words, a great blend of prim, proper and the freakishly bizarre...somebody pass the hookah, this one’s gonna get weird. <br/><br/>Set in 1861 in an <s>Victorian</s> Albertian England, Mark Hodder has created one of the most enticingly strange and intriguing steampunk worlds I have come a</span>
  <span id="freeText5902805253272671695" style="display:none">This super debut novel is like a sweet, dainty cup of mild <b>English tea</b>...if it was spiked with <b>Absinthe</b>, poured into a <b>heavy brass goblet</b> and served with <b>Laudanum-laced</b> cookies shaped like medical experiments gone awry. In other words, a great blend of prim, proper and the freakishly bizarre...somebody pass the hookah, this one’s gonna get weird. <br /><br />Set in 1861 in an <s>Victorian</s> Albertian England, Mark Hodder has created one of the most enticingly strange and intriguing steampunk worlds I have come across in my literary travels. Charles Darwin has all but murdered religion, London is choking on the pollution that is the byproduct of its runaway industrial innovations and the parliament-controlled government is a powder-keg of factions. <br /><br />The Technologists create modern marvels ranging from brass robots, mechanical trash-burning litter-crabs and one-man flying contraptions called “rotochairs.” The Eugenicists splice and tinker to create specialized, genetically-engineered species to act cheap labor. Both of these two group bear much in common with the “Clankers” and the “Darwinists” from Scott Westerfeld’s excellent YA "Leviathan" series, though there is a much more gothic, Vandermeer/Mieville feel to them in this work. <br /><br />Socially, we have the Libertines who adhere to a morally dubious celebration of freedom calling for a society without restrictive laws that celebrates beauty, art and the freeing of humanity from the burdens of social conventions. I dubbed these guys the <b>“Dorian Gray”</b> party, sans the creepy painting and a young Oscar Wilde is actually a character in the story. <br /><br />Finally, we have the “Rakes”....who take everything the libertines believe in and push it to eleven. They are darker, more sexually deviant and far more callous. Their dream is a world where humanity lives controlled by their primal instincts for sex, violence and anarchy and they inhabit much of the darker “criminal” enterprises in the city (i.e., drugs, sex clubs, etc..). <br /><br />In touring this world, we are guided by a pair of brash, roguish “gentlemen scoundrels” who may turn out to be outstanding leading characters in future novels. Sir Richard Francis Burton (yes...that one) is a famous explorer, scholar, swordsman and an extremely cunning-linguist. Algernon Charles Swinburne is a clever, morally casual libertine poet who has a serious pain fetish and digs nothing more than a really firm flogging of the bottom...or anywhere else for that matter. By the way, Algy is also a serious drunkard, but I don’t feel qualified to judge on this point...<i>‘He who is without a hangover can cast the first shot glass’</i>...or something like that. <br /><br />So here’s the plot lowdown:<br /><br /><b>
  <u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>
</b><br /><br />Despite Burton’s fame, he has fallen into disfavor after suffering a humiliating scandal perpetrated by a group that includes his oldest friend, John Hanning Speke. Richard returns to London unsure of what his future holds at the same time London is being harried by a legendary boogeyman and possible “would be rapist” known as Spring-heeled Jack. After a bizarre encounter with this mysterious apparition, Burton is hired as a special agent of <s>Prince</s> King Albert to solve the mystery of the entity’s strange appearances. <br /><br />At the same time, a group of child-stealing <b>loup-garous</b> (aka, fancy talk for werewolves) are terrorizing the poorer sections of London and snatching young members of the League of Chimney Sweeps. Richard and his almost trusty sidekick Algy begin to wonder if the two series of events might be connected...What do they find?...uh, uh...that would be telling. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br /><br />In terms of ideas and plot, this book does not feel like a debut novel. This man has deft, story-crafting chops and is sure to make his presence felt in years to come. Except for a bit of slippage in the last 50 pages where the story seemed a bit out of control, Hodder maintains a firm grasp on his narrative. Also, he does something that I have never seen before in a steampunk novel. He provides a credible and understandable basis for exactly how such technology exists and doesn’t just ask the reader to accept it as a given. This explanation is part of the “big reveal” that takes place halfway through the story and sets this one well above the norm in terms of inventiveness and plot lay out. <br /><br />There are some things the book could have done better. I loved the two main characters, but I thought they could have been a little better developed. However, as there is already a sequel with a third book coming out soon, I am confident that both Burton’s and Swinburne’s characters will be filled in and expanded. Also, as wonderfully put together as the plot was, I thought the very end was a bit rushed and felt a little like Hodder had to tourniquet the climax because he was afraid of story gush and needed to get things tied off and wrapped up. <br /><br />Still, an incredibly impressive debut. Quality prose, very engaging characters, a superbly, SUPERBLY imagined world and terrific central story involving a who blend of SF tropes that come together into a wonderful stew. <br /><br />4.0 t0 4.5 stars. HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5902805253272671695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9647949-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=i-trust-irena">i-trust-irena</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer789273025" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14250811275385459588"><b>"Book, you have the right to a speedy trial"</b> review<br/> <br/><i>
  <b>THE DEFENSE</b>
</i><br/> - A brilliant reimagining of several historical figures. <br/> - Loved how philosophical themes like <i>"technology vs. humanity"</i> and <i>"propriety vs. freedom"</i> were explored. <br/> - Exemplary world-building and atmosphere throughout. <br/> - Author succeeds where so many other sci-fi writers have failed, he manages to explore alternate timelines without being confusing at all! <br/> - Swinburne is especially entertaining!<br/> <br/><i>
  <b>THE PROSECUTION</b>
</i><br/> - Not enou</span>
  <span id="freeText14250811275385459588" style="display:none"><b>"Book, you have the right to a speedy trial"</b> review<br /> <br /><i>
  <b>THE DEFENSE</b>
</i><br /> - A brilliant reimagining of several historical figures. <br /> - Loved how philosophical themes like <i>"technology vs. humanity"</i> and <i>"propriety vs. freedom"</i> were explored. <br /> - Exemplary world-building and atmosphere throughout. <br /> - Author succeeds where so many other sci-fi writers have failed, he manages to explore alternate timelines without being confusing at all! <br /> - Swinburne is especially entertaining!<br /> <br /><i>
  <b>THE PROSECUTION</b>
</i><br /> - Not enough Swinburne!<br /> - Lengthy descriptions of steampunk contraptions occasionally left me glassy-eyed.<br /> - Horrific moments (particularly Spring Heeled Jack's targeting of young women) may be too much for some readers.<br /> - More significant female characters would have been nice... the book is pretty much one gigantic sausage fest! <br /> <br /><i>
  <b>THE VERDICT</b>
</i><br />Whereas other steampunk novels choose to only graze at real-life events (i.e. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6050678.Leviathan__Leviathan___1_" title="Leviathan (Leviathan, #1) by Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Leviathan</a>) or create a new world entirely (i.e. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6285903.Retribution_Falls__Tales_of_the_Ketty_Jay___1_" title="Retribution Falls (Tales of the Ketty Jay, #1) by Chris Wooding" rel="nofollow noopener">Retribution Falls</a>), Mark Hodder realizes the fullest potential of the steampunk genre, blending several historical figures and events together to create a fascinating alternate reality. While some parts of the story are disturbing enough to make even George R R Martin cringe, the novel remains unputdownable throughout. Can't wait for the next installment!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616142407" href="/book/show/8181143-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=i-gave-up">i-gave-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=fog-and-gears">fog-and-gears</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265319742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8973241039447491046">EH? EH! this desperate steampunk non-adventure plays like an overly hysterical farce with delusions of grandeur. although seemingly full of creative ideas, those ideas have run sadly amuck. there is no grounding of the frivolity within interesting characterization or sparkling dialogue - both of which remain almost obstinately insipid and amateurish; famous english personages are tossed around willy-nilly with little sense and zero resonance; cutesie-poo preciousness is found everywhere, from th</span>
  <span id="freeText8973241039447491046" style="display:none">EH? EH! this desperate steampunk non-adventure plays like an overly hysterical farce with delusions of grandeur. although seemingly full of creative ideas, those ideas have run sadly amuck. there is no grounding of the frivolity within interesting characterization or sparkling dialogue - both of which remain almost obstinately insipid and amateurish; famous english personages are tossed around willy-nilly with little sense and zero resonance; cutesie-poo preciousness is found everywhere, from the lil' newsboy Oscar Wilde to foul-mouthed delivery parrots; "steampunk elements" themselves are parroted on an ad hoc basis but have little internal logic, only inspiring sighs &amp; eye-rolling from this severely disappointed and agitated reader. at a little over the halfway mark (@ page 200, i think), i decided my time had been wasted enough and chose to skim the rest - if only to see how Hodder dealt with his inexplicably villainous creations Charles Darwin &amp; Florence Nightingale. although they turned out to be a disappointment, i'm glad i chose skimming instead of tossing. the final third of the novel contains a rather awesome, multi-chapter novel-within-a-novel that details the sad, terrible, increasingly fearful misadventures of the titular, time-traveling, so-called villain "Spring Heeled Jack". now THAT portion of the novel was marvelous. certainly worthy of at least one extra star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8973241039447491046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_135436493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135436493" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135436493?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616142407" href="/book/show/8181143-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=forty-for-2012-personal-challenge">forty-for-2012-personal-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fantasy">sci-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=new-novella">new-novella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135436493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10236305590891320540">I'm sitting here trying to decide how to say what I need to say about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7293120.The_Strange_Affair_of_Spring_Heeled_Jack__Burton___Swinburne___1_' title='The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack (Burton & Swinburne, #1) by Mark Hodder' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack</a>, and I can't get my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/221253.Cherie_Priest' title='Cherie Priest' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cherie Priest</a>’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99890392' rel='nofollow noopener'>Boneshaker</a> out of my head. So I'm going let it inspire me:<br/><br/>I dug <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3222611.Mark_Hodder' title='Mark Hodder' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mark Hodder</a>’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7293120.The_Strange_Affair_of_Spring_Heeled_Jack__Burton___Swinburne___1_' title='The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack (Burton & Swinburne, #1) by Mark Hodder' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Strange Affair of Spring-heeled Jack</a>, but it was too damn much. <br/><br/>I dug Albertan England, but the changes from the Victorian England I am familiar with were too outrageous, too far beyond what even my whacked-out imagination could accept.<br/><br/>I dug the <i>loups-garous</i>, b</span>
  <span id="freeText10236305590891320540" style="display:none">I'm sitting here trying to decide how to say what I need to say about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7293120.The_Strange_Affair_of_Spring_Heeled_Jack__Burton___Swinburne___1_" title="The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack (Burton &amp; Swinburne, #1) by Mark Hodder" rel="nofollow noopener">The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack</a>, and I can't get my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/221253.Cherie_Priest" title="Cherie Priest" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherie Priest</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99890392" rel="nofollow noopener">Boneshaker</a> out of my head. So I'm going let it inspire me:<br /><br />I dug <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3222611.Mark_Hodder" title="Mark Hodder" rel="nofollow noopener">Mark Hodder</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7293120.The_Strange_Affair_of_Spring_Heeled_Jack__Burton___Swinburne___1_" title="The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack (Burton &amp; Swinburne, #1) by Mark Hodder" rel="nofollow noopener">The Strange Affair of Spring-heeled Jack</a>, but it was too damn much. <br /><br />I dug Albertan England, but the changes from the Victorian England I am familiar with were too outrageous, too far beyond what even my whacked-out imagination could accept.<br /><br />I dug the <i>loups-garous</i>, but there were too many of them, and their spontaneous wolf-man combustion was one pseudo-Sci-Fi step too far for me to suspend my disbelief. <br /><br />I dug Sir Richard Burton and Algernon Swinburne, and even Speke and Palmerston (plastic face and all) were tolerable, but throwing in Charles Darwin, Florence Nightingale, Ismabard Kingdom Brunel stretched my ability to cope. But even that wasn't enough for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3222611.Mark_Hodder" title="Mark Hodder" rel="nofollow noopener">Hodder</a>. No, no, no. He had to give us a newsboy, nicknamed Quips (so clever), who just happens to be a young Oscar Wilde. But even THAT wasn't enough for Hodder. Nope. The revelation of Wilde's identity came upon his first meeting with a poet named Algy a couple of paragraphs away from the books only use of the word "perambulator." Fuck off. <br /><br />I dug the "new novella" at the heart of the tale -- <i>Part Two: Being the True History of Spring Heeled Jack</i> -- and would love to have seen all of Hodder's energy poured into that history. As a novella, it might have been nearly as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/880695.H_G__Wells" title="H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">H.G. Wells</a>' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17184.The_Invisible_Man_" title="The Invisible Man  by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The Invisible Man</a>, but then there's Part One and Three and the Conclusion and the Appendix, and there is an excess of plot and action that is just begging to be streamlined and morphed into a radio play (odd, I know, but I kept hearing the story in my head with the crackling overlay of an old-time radio). I wanted to mess with it and adapt it, or beg Hodder to keep it simple and short, but he was too in love with his own cleverness, and that hurt the literary experience (if not the entertainment experience).<br /><br />I dug The Mad Marquess and even dug his Mr. Belljar alter-ego, but the way he became the damn dirty ape of Burton's nightmares was ... well ... lame because of everything (such as Ms. Nightengale) that was required to make it work.<br /><br />I dug Spring Heeled Jack, and I loved the way we watched his loose-ends tie up, but I wanted him to be smarter than he was. Perhaps that's not fair, though.<br /><br />I dug how Burton finished the tale and made a timeline shaking choice based purely on his selfish desires, but I don’t buy for a second that it was required. The timeline was already irrevocably fucked. Still, "heroic" brutality was refreshing, and it made him feel more like James Bond than Sherlock Holmes. <br /><br />I dug most of the technological steampunk elements, but I grew thoroughly weary of the eugenic steampunk elements. Again, Wells did it better when he was writing straight up Sci-Fi in the Victorian Era than any steampunk writers can do today when they ape the era for their stories. Herbert George, what would you make of steampunk?<br /><br />I dug the hint of more tales with Burton and Swinburne, but I think I would rather spend some time in Damascus with Isabel Arundell instead. <br /><br />I dug <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7293120.The_Strange_Affair_of_Spring_Heeled_Jack__Burton___Swinburne___1_" title="The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack (Burton &amp; Swinburne, #1) by Mark Hodder" rel="nofollow noopener">The Strange Affair of Spring-heeled Jack</a>, but it was too much of a good thing and not enough of a great thing, and the only way to get to the great would have been to decrease the good because too much good winds up being just okay.<br /><br />I wonder if Burton and Swinburne will take on Jack the Ripper next? Seems appropriate, and what would the Ripper be in a timeline so fantastically altered? That could actually bring me back to Hodder's Albertan past. I'll cross my fingers and toes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10236305590891320540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2903449025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2903449025" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2903449025?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19306110-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2903449025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6018298018511831026"><i>The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack</i> is the first book in a steampunk series called “Burton & Swinburne”. This was a crazy, fun book. It’s kinda sorta set in the Victorian era and features many historical figures who are misused to serve the author’s evil purposes. I could imagine this book would surely drive some people crazy, but I really enjoyed it even while recognizing it has some flaws.<br/><br/>The main characters, Burton and Swinburne, are two of the aforementioned real people from history. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText6018298018511831026" style="display:none"><i>The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack</i> is the first book in a steampunk series called “Burton &amp; Swinburne”. This was a crazy, fun book. It’s kinda sorta set in the Victorian era and features many historical figures who are misused to serve the author’s evil purposes. I could imagine this book would surely drive some people crazy, but I really enjoyed it even while recognizing it has some flaws.<br /><br />The main characters, Burton and Swinburne, are two of the aforementioned real people from history. The story focuses mainly on Burton, but Swinburne plays more of a role eventually. Near the beginning of the book, Burton has returned to London after learning that a man he knew well has shot himself. While walking home drunk from a pub, he’s accosted by a strangely costumed man on spring-loaded stilts who leaps out of nowhere, beats him up, and yells at him to do what he’s supposed to do. Burton has never seen this man before and has no idea what he’s talking about.<br /><br />In addition to the steampunk-type technology, there are also genetically altered creatures. They’re a bit silly, but fun. I particularly enjoyed the potty-mouth parakeets; I’m not sure what that says about me! Of course, nothing could beat the broom cats. Has there ever been a cat owner in all of history who has NEVER tried to convince their cat to serve as a broom? This is probably why modern cats love Roombas so much. (Lest anybody read this book and end up horribly disappointed, broom cats do not play a significant role in this book. They’re just briefly mentioned.)<br /><br />This is probably not a book to read if unrealistic science bothers you. The genetic creations are pretty unlikely, and even the technological creations are more than a small stretch in the context of the story. The book might also bother people who want their historical figures to be portrayed consistent with how history portrays them. The history wasn’t much of a problem for me since I don’t know UK history well, and for the rest of it I found that I was able to suspend my disbelief pretty easily and just go with the flow. I found it a lot of fun, the story kept me interested as I worked to connect the scattered dots, and it made me laugh a lot. If I have one complaint, it was that people seemed to go off the deep end awfully easily, which made it difficult for me to buy into some of the characters' behaviors. Some of the characters did have experiences that would have been shocking and horrible to actually experience, yet I believe humans are more resilient than they were portrayed in this book.<br /><br />I did like that my edition had some brief explanations at the end of the book about both the real legend of spring heeled jack as well as the many historical figures who showed up in the book. I was a little bit overwhelmed in the very beginning by all of these characters who had wiki entries when I touched their names in my Kindle, because only a few were familiar to me. However, the character introductions eventually settled down and I was able to keep everybody straight. I didn’t worry too much about who they really were while I read the book, but I was more interested in reading that historical info at the end of the book after I had already spent a few hundred pages with their fictional counterparts.<br /><br />This book tells a complete story. I’m not sure if the setting can sustain my interest for an entire six-book series, but I enjoyed this first one well enough that I’m going to continue on to the second and see how things go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6018298018511831026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_337777536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337777536" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335664-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551667298p2/3335664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337777536?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3335664-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/13510250-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">sexy Indian nuns, time traveling perverts, poets who like a good birching</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=19th-century">19th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=british-literature">british-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337777536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5929508417427772835">Steampunk is all the rage nowadays. <i>The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack</i> seizes the trend in an intriguingly weird story that turns history on its head, thanks to the inept bungling of a time-traveler who, in our world, was one of the most notorious urban legends of Victorian England.<br/><br/>I am not really a huge fan of steampunk. Actually, to put it bluntly, I think most steampunk is stupid, an excuse to mix corsets and Anglophilia with science fiction.<br/><br/>But I enjoyed this book a lot. It's rip-roari</span>
  <span id="freeText5929508417427772835" style="display:none">Steampunk is all the rage nowadays. <i>The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack</i> seizes the trend in an intriguingly weird story that turns history on its head, thanks to the inept bungling of a time-traveler who, in our world, was one of the most notorious urban legends of Victorian England.<br /><br />I am not really a huge fan of steampunk. Actually, to put it bluntly, I think most steampunk is stupid, an excuse to mix corsets and Anglophilia with science fiction.<br /><br />But I enjoyed this book a lot. It's rip-roarin' well-plotted adventure, with a fine attention to historical detail if not scientific plausibility.<br /><br />There are lots of things Mark Hodder does right. His alt-history is a colorful blend of historical figures and fanciful inventions. It's not science, it's <b>Science!</b> When a time traveler from the 22nd century goes back in time to 1840, the date on which 18-year-old Edward Oxford attempted to assassinate Queen Victoria, he inadvertently causes the assassination to succeed. The changes that result from Victoria's death are not merely the loss of "Victorian" England, but a 19th century England in which Technologists build ornithopters and geothermal power stations and air trains, while eugenicists engineer messenger dogs and parakeets, house-cleaning cats, and elephantine horses. Meanwhile, Libertines and Rakes are rival factions preaching a complete overthrow of the social order. Mesmerism and other "magical" practices are real, and genetic engineering on humans is beginning.<br /><br />Adventuring, two-fisted pulp style, in this steampunk bizarro world are the famous explorer Sir Richard Francis Burton and the poet Algernon Swinburne. Burton crosses the sinister time-traveling "Spring Heeled Jack," thus becoming ensnared in his calamitous attempts to unscrew history.<br /><br />The use of actual historical figures is cleverly done. According to 19th century lore, Spring Heeled Jack was some sort of superhuman demi-rapist, running around England sexually assaulting women by tearing their clothes off. Hodder actually comes up with a logical explanation for "Jack's" behavior, and for how the loon could be a time traveler. I also appreciated his use of historical personages and events. Edward Oxford was a real person, and his attempted assassination of Queen Victoria is a historical fact; Hodder makes strange fiction out of it. He uses real people like Richard Burton, Algernon Swinburne, and Lord Henry Beresford of Waterford, with cameos by Oscar Wilde, Charles Babbage, and others. I was particularly amused at the eeeeeeevil evolutionists being led by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Charles Darwin and Florence Nightingale <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There was no insertion of overtly fictional characters — i.e., no Sherlock Holmes or Allan Quatermain. It's almost like a bent world that might have been.<br /><br />That said, this book gets 4 stars for story and content, 3 stars for writing. I suppose some of the writing tics that bugged me may have been a deliberate attempt to emulate the writing style of Victorian pulp adventures, hence Sir Richard Burton constantly being referred to as "the King's agent." But having long chapters of exposition narrated to us by the expedient of characters eavesdropping on the bad guys as they conveniently monologue their life history and then spell out their plans in detail? Lazy. Entertaining as heck, but lazy. Hodder is a great storyteller, and the pace never flagged, even during the monologues, but the plotting was sloppy. And like most steampunk settings, there's a lot of suspension of disbelief required, since steampunk cyborgs, talking orangutans, and genetically-engineered housepets are not a logical consequence of killing Queen Victoria, even with a time traveler letting slip a few hints about the future to inquisitive 19th century scientists. Still, accept that history has been kicked onto its side and anything goes, and the plot flows right along.<br /><br />A great read for any fan of steampunk, an entertaining read for fans of historicals who don't mind fantasy.<br /><br />Also, I must confess that this debut novel, which was wobbling a little shakily between 3 and 4 stars, earned its fourth star when it ended with my very favorite Swinburne poem:<br /><br /><blockquote><br />From too much love of living,<br /> From hope and fear set free,<br />We thank with brief thanksgiving<br /> Whatever gods may be<br />That no life lives for ever;<br />That dead men rise up never;<br />That even the weariest river<br /> Winds somewhere safe to sea.<br /></blockquote><br /><br />Good enough for me to consider the next volume in the series when I am in the mood for a beach read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5929508417427772835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1237081706" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237081706" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237081706?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237081706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11179195616982502292">This book was brilliant and one of the best books I have picked up in a while because of how vastly different it was, and yet thoroughly engrossing. I tend to read a lot of Epic or High Fantasy which is what I love to read, but this rings more as an adventure, Victorian-era fiction, Steampunk Fantasy and Sci-fi story all rolled into one. You may think that sounds like an awful lot of stuff, and it is, but it <i>works!</i><br/><br/>Having never heard of or read anything by Hodder prior to this I went into this wi</span>
  <span id="freeText11179195616982502292" style="display:none">This book was brilliant and one of the best books I have picked up in a while because of how vastly different it was, and yet thoroughly engrossing. I tend to read a lot of Epic or High Fantasy which is what I love to read, but this rings more as an adventure, Victorian-era fiction, Steampunk Fantasy and Sci-fi story all rolled into one. You may think that sounds like an awful lot of stuff, and it is, but it <i>works!</i><br /><br />Having never heard of or read anything by Hodder prior to this I went into this with a very open mind and no real expectations other than I loved the cover designs, and one of my friends gave it a 5* review so I knew it had to be decent. I didn't know what it was other than it was a kind of absurdist steampunk novel, and I certainly didn't think I would fall in love with it as much as I did.<br /><br />This is the story of a rather wacky world. It's kind of like our Victorian period, but it's also got a lot more cool inventions and some very comical characters. The author has clearly looked into people of the era who were influential and famous, and these make up the main part of the cast, however they do not act as they would have done in our world because the land that they live in is so different and wacky that their stories in this book are a lot more colourful and fun than their 'real--life' histories. <br /><br />This book has some exceptionally witty and truly wonderful writing. Whilst it doesn't swerve away from bold language in some scenes, there's always a sense that you're living and reading about the proper period of history and even with the added contraptions of the world, there's a distinct gentlemanly feeling which sort of echoes Sherlock. <br /><br />A large amount of this story focuses on two characters, Burton and Swinburne (as the title of the series would suggest). These two are pretty funny characters indeed with Burton being a famous explorer and the main protagonist, and Swinburne a semi-famous poet who is sort of a reluctantly accepted side-kick. These two make for some wonderful conversation and discourse, with a whole lot of charm and charisma thrown in too. They bounce well off of one another, and work well together as a team. I have to say that they were wonderful characters to get to know!<br /><br />I actually listened to this on audiobook largely and I have to say I think that the Narrator, Gerard Doyle, was fabulous at making this world yet more exhilarating and the characters far more apt to their roles and society than I could have imagined in my head. He did some stellar voice acting and I would highly recommend this as a series you may consider to listen to.<br /><br />However, equally another aspect which I loved about the physical edition was that at the start of every chapter we had something like a note, letter or advert which was either related to the story, characters or the world, and by far the adverts were my favourite. Over the course of this book we see a fair few absurd and hilarious advertisements and flyers with the appropriate embellishments of the time for all manner of bizarre and wonderful product such as motorised penny farthings to beard growing kits. It made me chuckle and smile every time I got to a new chapter!<br /><br />Finally, what is the story all about? Well this is a funny one to explain because although everything links up we actually have 3 parts to the book, the first focusing on Burton as he returns from and adventure to find that his friend and enemy has supposedly died, and everything he wanted in his life is severely shaken when he's assigned a role by appointment of the King. His story gets more and more crazy but suffice to say it eventually involves a rather deranged and wild character of Spring-Heeled Jack who is a vibrant, interesting and baffling character all at once. <br />The second part of the story focuses on a character called Oxford who becomes an interesting part of the story and tells his own version of events which we have already experienced with our initial character.<br />The final part was the convergence of both storylines, and I have to say I think the book was wonderfully structured and a lot of fun to read and experience!<br /><br />On the whole if you've never heard of or been interested in this book I would highly advise that you give it a look the next time you're out and about because this was certainly a book I adored and the start to what promises to be a wonderful series. A firm 5*s and I cannot wait to progress further with the next books as I do already own book 2 and 3 and can't wait to pick them up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11179195616982502292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1086945469" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1086945469" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532221628p2/23841736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1086945469?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22053384-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy-challenge-2016">sci-fi-fantasy-challenge-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=brilliant-narration">brilliant-narration</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086945469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4289648895133458059">I had to create a number of shelves to accommodate this wacky novel. It's primarily a Steampunk Victorian Detective Novel and then you add all of these other elements in. Rogue geneticists, time travel, the assassination of Queen Victoria, a mad Marquess (<i>very</i> Victorian), a timeline that goes increasingly awry, and my favorite bit, part swashbuckling adventure. I swear this book made me want to whip out a rapier and dance around like a mad lunatic. Which is what I would look like if I tried swor</span>
  <span id="freeText4289648895133458059" style="display:none">I had to create a number of shelves to accommodate this wacky novel. It's primarily a Steampunk Victorian Detective Novel and then you add all of these other elements in. Rogue geneticists, time travel, the assassination of Queen Victoria, a mad Marquess (<i>very</i> Victorian), a timeline that goes increasingly awry, and my favorite bit, part swashbuckling adventure. I swear this book made me want to whip out a rapier and dance around like a mad lunatic. Which is what I would look like if I tried sword-fighting. Oh, there's also a young Oscar Wilde as a newsboy. <br /><br />Burton is offered a job as the King's Agent at the beginning of the book and told to investigate the werewolf problem in London. After explaining to the Prime Minister that he was accosted the night before by a strange figure, Burton finds out that this is the famed mythical figure, Spring Heeled Jack. He's told to investigate that as well. I don't want to say anything else because it would be easy to spoiler something. I will say that there isn't much food for thought here but it's a hell of a lot of fun if that's what you're looking for. I'm looking forward to the rest of the series. Two things did surprise me. The author really captures the feel of a Victorian detective novel but he manages to somehow mix it with all of these strange elements without it ever seeming awkward. The other is that the author explained every single one of Spring Heeled Jack's appearances. That was impressive.<br /><br />Also, I listened to the audio and the narrator was beyond brilliant. He did an excellent range of voices, my favorite was the Beadle that lived in a chimney and protected the chimney sweeps. I was never clear on what he was exactly but the narrator's voice was hilariously spooky.<br /><br />This was a truly fun book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4289648895133458059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3029520645" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/3673987-mike">Mike</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3673987-mike?shelf=read-sf-award-winners">read-sf-award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3673987-mike?shelf=series-in-progress">series-in-progress</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3673987-mike?shelf=read-all-the-books-the-sixth-sense">read-all-the-books-the-sixth-sense</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3029520645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14949605029725488646">A really good steampunk-slash-alternate-history book, with an entertaining and plausible origin embedded in the story and some great characters. I'm going to refer folks over to friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party' rel='nofollow noopener'>David</a>'s review <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/789273025' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>, as his 5-star review captures most all of my feelings for this book. <br/><br/>My additional thoughts: <br/>- I was not quite as taken with Swineburne as he was -- there was just enough of the Algy character for me.<br/>- There was no logical reason for Quips to exist as he did in this story, which the author bas</span>
  <span id="freeText14949605029725488646" style="display:none">A really good steampunk-slash-alternate-history book, with an entertaining and plausible origin embedded in the story and some great characters. I'm going to refer folks over to friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party" rel="nofollow noopener">David</a>'s review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/789273025" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>, as his 5-star review captures most all of my feelings for this book. <br /><br />My additional thoughts: <br />- I was not quite as taken with Swineburne as he was -- there was just enough of the Algy character for me.<br />- There was no logical reason for Quips to exist as he did in this story, which the author basically confesses to in the end notes. Once I learned that he was superfluous, the story took a step down in quality for me.<br />- I didn't think some of the biological inventions could have occurred as early in history as they did here, both for the internal logic of the story, and for scientific reasons, although they were quite entertaining.<br />- The moral behavior of the protagonists seemed historically accurate. Those of their enemies seemed a bit overblown (although necessary to support the plot), so it gave an air of fantasy rather than science fiction. Not all of behavior of either side, however, was pleasant.<br /><br />Overall, quite good and worth the read. I hope the next in the series can keep up!<br /><br /><br />Monopoly "Steampunk" move.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_322758931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322758931" />
    <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes"><img alt="aPriL does feral sometimes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478243665p2/3409532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322758931?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616142407" href="/book/show/8181143-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=alt-universe">alt-universe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322758931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14025191958997455187">‘The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack’ is a madcap movie, basically, and entertaining, but without the inventions this is a three-star read, really. But if you unpack the novel, the entire story is a Rube Goldberg machine. I liked but not loved. I've given four stars because the author Mark Hodder was clever by throwing in real inventions from the mid-1880's and the plot posed some interesting dilemmas which occurred from time traveling. I had the most fun Googling the inventions and studyin</span>
  <span id="freeText14025191958997455187" style="display:none">‘The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack’ is a madcap movie, basically, and entertaining, but without the inventions this is a three-star read, really. But if you unpack the novel, the entire story is a Rube Goldberg machine. I liked but not loved. I've given four stars because the author Mark Hodder was clever by throwing in real inventions from the mid-1880's and the plot posed some interesting dilemmas which occurred from time traveling. I had the most fun Googling the inventions and studying the drawings. <br /><br />The oddness of everything draws you into the book and keeps you reading (or maybe it will put you off the book). Nothing is normal, but not too alarming. Everything is a bit off, literally and figuratively. This is an alternative universe story that takes place in 1861 London. It has famous people in history as protagonists, but these people could not have ever been as represented here in this novel. Basic physical features and personalities are vaguely acknowledged, but how they lived in history is completely rearranged into Frankenstein mash ups. Instead of the usual romantic London we have come to expect from Sherlock Holmes movies, this London is similar to the bottom of a mine or Manhatten on 9/11, full of soot, dirt, dust and airborne filth. Admirable qualities of the hero characters are muted, while their darker natures are what make them successful. Women are cosseted in theory while mistreated and disrespected in all the usual ways (the author didn't have to twist anything here, the real world's attitudes are sufficiently twisted 'as is'). Vehicles of Travel of all sorts seems to be an underlying but powerful theme, a lot of them being crackpot inventions that work; however, everyone moves in circles revisiting the same streets or move only in time while jumping up and down in the same spot.<br /><br />As a reader from 2012, in effect I'm a time travelor in the point-of-view position of the character Spring Heeled Jack. While he finds himself unable to accept his circumstances, I want to explore, examine and make friends with this world. Jack's feelings don't make sense to me. His costume is clownish, and the stilts that he has made necessary to the functioning of his invention is a peculiar way to solve the problem of its functioning. His time travel suit is a Rube Goldberg machine. In addition, his original quest is ridiculous considering the lengths he went to in order to change a long ago and ultimately minor historical note, but I suppose that's the nature of Rube Goldberg crackpots.<br /><br />The cascade of disrupted history and displaced technology is the fun part of the book. But again, it's off kilter in application to the story. The only part of society that is disrupted is some of the upper class, particularly those who are crackpots in philosophical and science matters.<br /><br />I think because the heart of the entire book is it's being an elaborate literary Rube Goldberg construction, I can't like it as much as I admire it. The off-kilter crackpot silliness overcomes this reader's ability to connect with anything emotionally. This alt-universe is ugly, too, despite the fact of everyone's either cheery soldiering on or stiff upper lip attitudes. Burton and Swinburne are not heroes, but bored dilettantes looking for something fun to do. They are not exactly haunted, but unhappy and unfulfilled. They both are rich, Burton more respectible and intellectually gifted while Swinburne fits the role of wing man. Burton, the 'hero' , is not a man burning with passion before, during or after events. For an explorer of harsh places, he is strangely unaffected by his discoveries, very one-dimensional. Swinburne is terrifically amusing, the only part of the book that had me laughing, but sadly, he is barely in the book. The werecreatures were appropriately monsterish and gory, so be warned graphic bits included.<br /><br />Is it worth reading? I think so. Is it likable? Maybe. I loved the broom cats and the message birds with coprolalia.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14025191958997455187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1008311120" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1008311120" />
    <a title="Mpauli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli"><img alt="Mpauli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373482375p2/8323869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1008311120?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mpauli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mpauli" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli">Mpauli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9647949-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=orga_read-in-2014">orga_read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=rating_5-stars">rating_5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_steampunk">genre_steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=orga_favourites">orga_favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=topic_werewolves">topic_werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=topic_philosophy">topic_philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=setting_london">setting_london</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1008311120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7827150933360952575">The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack is a clever mash-up of well researched history and the author's wide imagination.<br/><br/>It follows the historical figure of Sir Richard Francis Burton, who does become a king's agent in this novel. His job is to solve the mystery of Spring Heeled Jack, an apparition on stilts who's supposed to have attacked a few people, but is disregarded as a myth. During the novel the strange masochistic poet Algernon Swinburne starts to assist Burton with his investigation.<br/><br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText7827150933360952575" style="display:none">The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack is a clever mash-up of well researched history and the author's wide imagination.<br /><br />It follows the historical figure of Sir Richard Francis Burton, who does become a king's agent in this novel. His job is to solve the mystery of Spring Heeled Jack, an apparition on stilts who's supposed to have attacked a few people, but is disregarded as a myth. During the novel the strange masochistic poet Algernon Swinburne starts to assist Burton with his investigation.<br /><br />Although most readers won't have a problem to figure out the mystery of Spring Heeled Jack early on, the why and how is laid out pretty cleverly and the novel has one or two unexpected twists regarding its structure.<br /><br />Author Mark Hodder shows that he is really talented, is able to create some memorable characters and has a knack for the Victorian era and its themes.<br />Morality, especially in a world where Charles Darwin shattered the belief in god and creation, is one of the main themes of the novel and not only our heroes are struggling with it.<br />There are some interesting debates in here and as a former sociology/philosophy student, I was pleasently surprised to find some old arguments presented in a new context.<br /><br />Long story short, I had a blast with this book on more than one level and I'm pretty happy that there are at least 4 sequel novels, cause I really like to see what Mark Hodder does with his Steampunk sandbox and his characters.<br /><br />Oh, and here goes out an honorable mention at the end. It is the first piece of anything apart from Queen's song Bohemian Rhapsody, where I encountered the word "Bismillah!".</span>
  <a data-text-id="7827150933360952575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_886569762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/886569762" />
    <a title="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods"><img alt="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602607922p2/29163734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/886569762?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" href="/user/show/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods">Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616142407" href="/book/show/8181143-the-strange-affair-of-spring-heeled-jack">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer886569762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer233014168538892977">I love this rollicking British steampunk alt-history period action/mystery/spec fic novel. This was my second time reading it and I am pleased to report that it was just as thrilling as I remembered from the less-dicerning me of ten years ago. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3222611.Mark_Hodder' title='Mark Hodder' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mark Hodder</a> has created (or repurposed) an intriguing pulp hero worthy of his literary ancestors, the swarthy, scarred, well-travelled, fierce-faced, mesmeric, king's agent Richard Burton. The book is very British, very modern (despite it's 1860's setting)</span>
  <span id="freeText233014168538892977" style="display:none">I love this rollicking British steampunk alt-history period action/mystery/spec fic novel. This was my second time reading it and I am pleased to report that it was just as thrilling as I remembered from the less-dicerning me of ten years ago. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3222611.Mark_Hodder" title="Mark Hodder" rel="nofollow noopener">Mark Hodder</a> has created (or repurposed) an intriguing pulp hero worthy of his literary ancestors, the swarthy, scarred, well-travelled, fierce-faced, mesmeric, king's agent Richard Burton. The book is very British, very modern (despite it's 1860's setting), very fuckbonkers with its mad mix of aberrant technology, genetically altered animals, historical figures and legends, and every other element masterfully pieced together here. <br /><br />The cast is heavy on males; the few female characters are fierce but restrained to varying degrees by the social systems of 19th-century England, one historical factor that was not altered for this book. This could be a downside for some readers. If you are an impatient reader, too, the early portions of the book might come across as dry. There is some info-dumping, skillfully done within the book's context but still, there is a lot of background information needed to get on with the main plot. At two fifths of the way into the book, though, there are plenty of explosions of action and furthering of core mysteries to make it worth sticking around at least that far. <br /><br />I love the book design (the Pyr paperback edition anyway) with its dynamic cover art, extended title (Mark Hodder presents Burton &amp; Swinburne in The Strange Affair of Spring Heeled Jack), interior design, and the chapter intro texts including in-world period-inspired ads and poetry and quotes from the book's characters. <br /><br />I first encountered this series in 2010 when my good wife picked out the second book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9740847.The_Curious_Case_of_the_Clockwork_Man__Burton___Swinburne___2_" title="The Curious Case of the Clockwork Man (Burton &amp; Swinburne, #2) by Mark Hodder" rel="nofollow noopener">The Curious Case of the Clockwork Man</a>, for me from the public library based on the cover, which does not make it clear that it was part 2 in a series. I read that, then came back to the first book, then the third, and was very surprised in a later year to see that there were further books because the story was fully encapsulated in the first three books. I only ever made it to book four before deciding that I wanted to start over at the beginning, and over time acquired copies of the whole series. This book sat for many months in my bedside to-read stack, continually cycling down to make time for library loans. Now, in the time of cholera, I am glad that I finally moved it back to the top of the pile. I am certain that I will enjoy the rest of the series and can't wait to see what the final volumes will bring.</span>
  <a data-text-id="233014168538892977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18078042887332066873" style="display:none">The Spring Heeled Jack novel that introduces an alt-history England of the early 1860's with a steampunk flavor and features Richard Burton as main hero who becomes a "special agent" of the king - among other changes Queen Victoria is assassinated in 1840 - with Algernon Swinburne as a sort of sidekick, while many notables like Darwin, Brunel, Oscar Wilde have cameos is for most part an unstable mixture of the modern Victoriana - a bit of a misnomer as above but still - (Lazarus Club, Meaning of Night, Drood) and steampunk Victoriana (Affinity Bridge, Bookman) with occasional descent in farcical grotesque, but a fast pace and an intriguing hero in Sir Richard keeps the book quite interesting. <br /><br />Then about 2/3 in the author takes a gamble - which is foreshadowed early so it did not come as a surprise per se for me, but its extreme importance in the structure of the book was a surprise - and starts explaining things by turning the novel into more of a sf one and for me at least it worked very well managing to balance the two modes that previously did not work so well together; there is still some slapstick farce here and there that annoyed me a little (villain fighting the hero and both declaiming stuff..) but the last third raises the game one level; an A to A+ and I hope we will see more of Burton/Swinburne and the fascinating universe the author created</span>
